<div id="review_2291745505" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2291745505" />
    <a title="Dianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2947323-dianne"><img alt="Dianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914767p2/2947323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291745505?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dianne" href="/user/show/2947323-dianne">Dianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/37642916-beneath-a-scarlet-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2947323-dianne?shelf=best-of-2018">best-of-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291745505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2770509254739565618">I enjoyed this suspenseful World War II story set in Italy under Nazi occupation. I love WWII fiction and don't believe I have ever read a book from the Italian perspective. The author makes it clear in the preface that this is not a biography or historical novel, but a work of fiction based on the life of Pino Lella. With that firmly in my mind, I didn't really mind Sullivan's embellishments to Lella's story, although it did seem as though Lella was personally present at every single significan</span>
  <span id="freeText2770509254739565618" style="display:none">I enjoyed this suspenseful World War II story set in Italy under Nazi occupation. I love WWII fiction and don't believe I have ever read a book from the Italian perspective. The author makes it clear in the preface that this is not a biography or historical novel, but a work of fiction based on the life of Pino Lella. With that firmly in my mind, I didn't really mind Sullivan's embellishments to Lella's story, although it did seem as though Lella was personally present at every single significant historical event in Italy between 1943 and 1945. Busy guy!<br /><br />My favorite part of the novel was the beginning, when Pino was in the Alps with Father Re. I thought Sullivan did a great job with the beautiful Alpine setting and creating tension as Pino helped Italian Jews escape into Switzerland. That alone would have been a great story. My least favorite part was the love story between Pino and Anna. I don't know why, but it felt more like a teenager's fantasy than a real love affair.<br /><br />One other thing that I thought was odd - this novel feels very much like young adult fiction. The writing was quite juvenile, as though it was written to that audience. I don't know if Sullivan did that deliberately to make it sound more like the teen-aged Lella's thoughts or if that's just his writing syle. It didn't work for me - I wish the writing had been less prosaic and more lyrical, or at least geared toward more mature readers.<br /><br />Still, the story is the thing here and it was hard to put the book down. A 3 for the writing and a 4 for the story. If you want a more accurate account of Lella's life, you can always look it up online, which I always do anyway after reading historical fiction. By the way, this is going to be a movie with Tom Holland (the new Spiderman) in the lead role. I think this could be an amazing movie!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2770509254739565618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2246888146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2246888146" />
    <a title="Stephanie Anze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27117957-stephanie-anze"><img alt="Stephanie Anze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604709893p2/27117957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2246888146?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Anze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Anze" href="/user/show/27117957-stephanie-anze">Stephanie Anze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27117957-stephanie-anze?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2246888146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6232541943527513586">Pino Lella was a typical teenager coming of age in Milan when the Nazis started their rampage. Afraid for their safety, Pino and his brother Mimo were sent by their parents to the countryside to Casa Alpina (a school for boys run by Catholic priests). Pino though can not sit idly and soon is involved in the underground resistance helping Jews get to Switzerland. Almost eighteen years old, Pino is signed up with the German army and unexpectadly finds a job as a driver for General Hans Leyers, Hit</span>
  <span id="freeText6232541943527513586" style="display:none">Pino Lella was a typical teenager coming of age in Milan when the Nazis started their rampage. Afraid for their safety, Pino and his brother Mimo were sent by their parents to the countryside to Casa Alpina (a school for boys run by Catholic priests). Pino though can not sit idly and soon is involved in the underground resistance helping Jews get to Switzerland. Almost eighteen years old, Pino is signed up with the German army and unexpectadly finds a job as a driver for General Hans Leyers, Hitler's right hand in Italy. Pino is tasked with espying on the general and relaying any intel to the resistance. Despite the risks, Pino accepts and his brave act will remain unknown.<br /><br />Dealing with WWII, Italy and the Nazi regime this is one thoroughly researched historical fiction book. Pino Lella's life takes a dramatic turn when he becomes the driver to General Leyers, Hitler's right hand in Italy. While its an ideal position to spy, its also a very dangerous one. Having helped smuggle Jews to Switzerland, Pino is not new to helping the resistance but he'll have to don a swastika to be of help this time around. Despite his young age, Pino looks at the greater good. A compelling and inspirational narrative, this book was quite appealing to me. When it comes to Italy and WWII, the history is somewhat bare in comparison to that of other countries. While I love the narrative, I did feel the book to be too long and the prose was not always precise. Still, this is a strong work and I would recommend it.<br /><br />Pino Lella remained quiet for sixty years about his war experience. Not even his wifes knew (Pino was married twice). It was upon learning about Pino that author Mark Sullivan traveled to Italy and interviewed him. Mr. Lella felt shame for having worn the infamous Nazi symbol in order to spy not realizing the sheer courage it took to take on such a task. Sullivan spent ten years on this book, travelling to Italy and Germany multiple times to verify information. Most people and events in this book are real but due to lack of paperwork and the pass of time some of the content had to be filled by Sullivan (Sullivan originally wanted this to be a work of nonfiction). Pino led quite an interesting life following the war. He sold luxury cars in Beverly Hills (and was quite adept at driving them too), he became a ski instructor and met James Dean, Gary Cooper and Ernest Hemingway. His greatest achievement though, is his role as spy in the war. His bravery is admirable and he is a true hero. Thanks to Mr. Sullivan for bringing his story to the forefront. Its reported that the movie rights of the book have been sold with Tom Holland to play the lead. Will be looking forward to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6232541943527513586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2319799777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319799777" />
    <a title="MarytheBookLover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3458404-marythebooklover"><img alt="MarytheBookLover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550871728p2/3458404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319799777?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MarytheBookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MarytheBookLover" href="/user/show/3458404-marythebooklover">MarytheBookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/35048585-beneath-a-scarlet-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3458404-marythebooklover?shelf=2018-favorites">2018-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3458404-marythebooklover?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319799777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7301675001830770666">My Opinion:<br/>This was a brilliantly written, and brutally honest book of one man's life in WW2. He went from being a child to becoming a man, a spy, a friend, and a lover. This tale is so emotional and heart wrenching that you can't help but fall in love with every minute of this book. WOW, just WOW. I can't even imagine going and doing any of these things. This was so well written and the tale told so well and with such emotion, it left me speechless. I don't even know how to explain this book or</span>
  <span id="freeText7301675001830770666" style="display:none">My Opinion:<br />This was a brilliantly written, and brutally honest book of one man's life in WW2. He went from being a child to becoming a man, a spy, a friend, and a lover. This tale is so emotional and heart wrenching that you can't help but fall in love with every minute of this book. WOW, just WOW. I can't even imagine going and doing any of these things. This was so well written and the tale told so well and with such emotion, it left me speechless. I don't even know how to explain this book or give it the justice it deserves. I don't think I know the right words for it, but I will try my best.<br /><br />This tale is about a boy of 17 years old that was helping jewish people escape the nazis during WW2. He would take them over the Alps and into Switzerland. These are death defining mountains that he took regular people like me and you through to survive. TO SURVIVE!!! He did this for many months and then came his time to enlist with the Nazis or to become a rebel (partisan) against them. With the help of his father and uncle he makes his choice and became a Nazis and then became a spy. His life was always in peril because of this and did not tell many what he was doing. He wasn't allowed to tell many including his brother for fear of anyone being tortured for it. <br /><br />The fighting, the plight of the slaves, the peril of being discovered. This book just emotionally has you hooked. It lacked all the gore, but not the depth of what he saw during his time as a soldier. Amazing tale of about 2 years of being a hero both in helping people escape through the Alps and being a spy in the Nazis army for the resistance. I cried several times during this tale. The fingers of the child, the starvation, the woman's plea, Anna, Carleto and for Pino himself. The firing squad. Oh, god..This book is just so amazing. AMAZING.<br /><br />Just so you know I do not usually read biographies or WW2 books or war books at all. So, for this to have me enthralled and loving it, says something about this book. I feel in love with Pino and his family and Father Re. Wonderful book, brilliantly written and a must read book. Get it, you will not be disappointed!<br /><br /><br />I give this book 5 of 5 stars!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=audio">audio</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566180184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11686617769003723139"><b>5 STARS</b> for content and <b>3 STARS</b> for the writing.<br/>Rounding up to <b>4 STARS</b> on this one!<br/><br/><b>What an impressive history of survival, grief and love!</b><br/><br/><b>Beneath a Scarlet Sky</b> is based on the true story of Pino Lella who lived in Milan, Italy and was a spy for the Allies. Before he was a spy, he was working underground and helping Jews escape over the Alps. After doing this for a year or two, his parents forced him to enlist as a German soldier.<br/><br/>In order to strike back against his Italian parents, he decides to </span>
  <span id="freeText11686617769003723139" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b> for content and <b>3 STARS</b> for the writing.<br />Rounding up to <b>4 STARS</b> on this one!<br /><br /><b>What an impressive history of survival, grief and love!</b><br /><br /><b>Beneath a Scarlet Sky</b> is based on the true story of Pino Lella who lived in Milan, Italy and was a spy for the Allies. Before he was a spy, he was working underground and helping Jews escape over the Alps. After doing this for a year or two, his parents forced him to enlist as a German soldier.<br /><br />In order to strike back against his Italian parents, he decides to join the resistance and fight the Nazi’s. He ends up turning into a spy and becomes the personal driver for General Hans Leyers. General Leyers was one of the Third Reich’s most powerful commanders operating out of Northern Italy. Leyers was involved with war strategy, weapons and infrastructure. He was one of Hitler's top men.<br /><br /><b>What guts Pino Lella had to live this double sided life!</b><br />I really enjoyed the story and content of this book. It was an amazing life he led during the war.<br /><br />The only thing that I found lacking was the writing.<br />I did not think that <i>Mark Sullivan’s</i> writing was that epic. It was okay but if he’d wrote a less interesting story, I’m not sure I would have stuck with it.<br />At the end of this book, I should have been a hot mess with tears streaming down my face, but I wasn’t.<br />I'm not sure what was lacking about the writing, but it didn’t evoke pain, sadness or rage in me. I definitely had rage when Auschwitz was brought up, along with the hunting and killing of millions of Jews, disabled people and anyone fighting the Nazi's.<br /><br />But back to the writing. It was just <b>okay</b>. I guess that’s still better then terrible!<br /><br />Thank you real life book club for picking this for the month. I learned a lot more about WWII reading this book. The story was fascinating, and I was in awe of all the people that fought against the Nazi regime!!<br /><br /><b>Recommended for fans of historical fiction and WWII history buffs!</b></span>

<div id="review_3274882344" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3274882344" />
    <a title="Lewis Weinstein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2231715-lewis-weinstein"><img alt="Lewis Weinstein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501879p2/2231715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3274882344?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lewis Weinstein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lewis Weinstein" href="/user/show/2231715-lewis-weinstein">Lewis Weinstein</a>

  <span id="freeText11639741934149928394" style="display:none">This is a magnificent read from beginning to end, and past the end to the epilogue that tells what happened to all the real-life characters ... action, emotion, reflection, mystery, suspense, passion ... bigger than life in many ways but still believable ... a very well-structured and well-written story based on true events not recorded until 70+ years after ...<br /><br />UPDATE *** As is my habit, I did not read the other GR reviews before writing my own ... Wow, was I surprised ... the diversity of opinion is remarkable ... I don't remember seeing a book with so many good and bad reviews ... but the bad reviews do not lead me to change mine; I liked the book, which I approached as a novel and not a memoir ... sure there were many coincidences, some not fully believable, but they all served to allow the author to portray powerful events though the lens of his "fictional character" ... it's a novel!</span>

<div id="review_1985294134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1985294134" />
    <a title="Marialyce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1277371-marialyce"><img alt="Marialyce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601165932p2/1277371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1985294134?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marialyce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marialyce" href="/user/show/1277371-marialyce">Marialyce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781503902374" href="/book/show/38321944-beneath-a-scarlet-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1277371-marialyce?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1985294134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4191021649141456565">3 I so wished I could have loved it stars<br/>5 stars for the bravery that Pino and others showed<br/><br/>This should have been a book I adored. It had all the elements of what I so enjoy in my books, heroes, World War 2, courage, nobility in the face of devastation and yet this novel left me feeling oddly displeased.<br/><br/>This is the story of a seventeen year old young man living in Italy during the war. He is sent away because his parents fear for his and his bother's safety. They are sent to a school in the Alps</span>
  <span id="freeText4191021649141456565" style="display:none">3 I so wished I could have loved it stars<br />5 stars for the bravery that Pino and others showed<br /><br />This should have been a book I adored. It had all the elements of what I so enjoy in my books, heroes, World War 2, courage, nobility in the face of devastation and yet this novel left me feeling oddly displeased.<br /><br />This is the story of a seventeen year old young man living in Italy during the war. He is sent away because his parents fear for his and his bother's safety. They are sent to a school in the Alps run by Catholic priests. The boys are eventually asked to embark on missions to help secret Jews away to Switzerland. The job these boys understood was not only dangerous because of the weather, the climbing, and the Nazis, but it also required the boys to be physically and mentally strong and agile. Pino and Mimo gladly accept the task and they guide many Jews to safety. When Pino approaches his eighteenth birthday, his parents call him home from the school fearing the draft, knowing that the Italian army will send him to fight in Russia which was certain death. They have him enlist in the Nazi army and it is through his facility with languages that he becomes a driver for General Leyes, a powerful Nazi.<br /><br />Pino Lella and his brother were true heroes and while Pino went on to be a spy while being the driver of a high ranking Nazi general, Mimo eventually joins the resistance. Of course what Pino is doing must be hidden so many of his friends and even relatives abhor his being a Nazi. He, at many times is the recipient of scorn and hatred. The war continues, Pino finds the girl, Anna, working as a maid for the mistress of General Leyes. He had been attracted to her previously. Anna and Pino connect, fall in love, and become lovers.<br /><br />The tension and the possibility of Pino's capture and the secrets he carries to his aunt and uncle makes for the bulk of the book. We learn of what he has witnessed, the transportation of the Jews to Auschwitz, the murders committed and the brutality of the Nazi overlords, the robbing of the Italian treasury, the robbing of Italian treasures and the taking of lives of the innocent. <br /><br />So why did this book fall flat for me? I have to think that sometimes an author tries too hard to cram every thought, every deed, every moment into a story. For me, that often makes for a read that I find overburdened with wordiness. What Pino and others did was amazing on so many levels. Their courage, their ability to face adversity was awe inspiring. I just wish the author had been able to inspire that awe in me.<br /><br />Thank you to my local library for purchasing this book for all to read.<br />You can find my reviews at my blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpress.com/">https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpres...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4191021649141456565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2128545329" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2128545329" />
    <a title="Nikki (Saturday Nite Reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1347292-nikki-saturday-nite-reader"><img alt="Nikki (Saturday Nite Reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582550067p2/1347292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2128545329?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki (Saturday Nite Reader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki (Saturday Nite Reader)" href="/user/show/1347292-nikki-saturday-nite-reader">Nikki (Saturday Nite Reader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/35048585-beneath-a-scarlet-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347292-nikki-saturday-nite-reader?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347292-nikki-saturday-nite-reader?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347292-nikki-saturday-nite-reader?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128545329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9347839208289379018"><i>Beneath a Scarlet Sky</i>, by Mark T. Sullivan, was inspired by the real life story of WWII hero, Pino Lella. This book was 10 years in the making for author, Mark T. Sullivan, whom met Pinot by chance and knew he wanted to tell his story. It is a work of fiction, but has been rumored to be about 90% true.<br/><br/>First things first, this audiobook is a commitment. It is 17 hours long! About 25% way through I upped the speed to 1.25x and it cut a few hours off, phew. I am terribly bad at paying attention to </span>
  <span id="freeText9347839208289379018" style="display:none"><i>Beneath a Scarlet Sky</i>, by Mark T. Sullivan, was inspired by the real life story of WWII hero, Pino Lella. This book was 10 years in the making for author, Mark T. Sullivan, whom met Pinot by chance and knew he wanted to tell his story. It is a work of fiction, but has been rumored to be about 90% true.<br /><br />First things first, this audiobook is a commitment. It is 17 hours long! About 25% way through I upped the speed to 1.25x and it cut a few hours off, phew. I am terribly bad at paying attention to audiobooks, but I do find I am most engaged in listening and not being distracted by everything around me (look a squirrel!) when I am taking a long drive. During a long weekend I went to visit friends in CT (about a 2 hour drive) so it was a perfect time to dive into Pino’s story.<br /><br />Pino is an Italian who at the age of 18 is forced to enlist to fight with the Germans on his home turf. Just the previous winter he was helping Jews escape to Switzerland, so you can imagine the pain Pinot is fighting internally to be working for the enemy.<br /><br />I am not one to give too much detailed information in my reviews, as I want the reader/listener to experience much of the granular details on their own. What I will say is that like any story about war, it is depressing. There is only so much one person can experience and it was wild to hear that much of this story was true for Pino. His love for Anna Marta will make you weep. He is witness to such destruction and devastation at a young age and still finds the strength to keep going. After listening to this audiobook all I wanted to do was find Pino and hug him (if you know anything about me, this is huge. I hate hugs, so for me to want to actually give one away…well that’s major).<br /><br />If you are taking a long drive, or can pay attention better than me, <i>Beneath a Scarlet Sky</i> is a solid historical fiction audiobook choice. You must commit your time, but it’s one worth experiencing. The writing is beautiful, great character development. There is also an epilogue that provides a snapshot of where many of these characters wound up in real life.<br /><br />The narrator, Will Damron, did an amazing job at tackling the various accents and character emotions. It was not an easy feat, but he made it sound easy.<br /><br />Also, super cool to note: it is soon to be a major motion picture, staring Tom Holland as Pino.<br /><br />To read my interview with Narrator, Will Damron visit: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://saturdaynitereader.com/2018/01/28/audiobook-review-narrator-interview-beneath-a-scarlet-sky-by-mark-t-sullivan/">https://saturdaynitereader.com/2018/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9347839208289379018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SsSAqvOL1STLPowmQdyt+sCGjgt1KdNEcoi2sqOTm+7c8eASNtsCvJDuyCFdtpNU7OcDhmdePdCie3YWEjH2xg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2113844088820888881">Mark T. Sullivan (b. 1958) is an author of thrillers. Born in a Boston suburb, he joined the Peace Corp after college, traveling to West Africa to live with a tribe of Saharan nomads. Upon returning to the United States, he took a job at Reuters, beginning a decade-long career in journalism that would eventually lead to a job as an investigative reporter for the San Diego Tribune.<br/><br/>Sullivan spent th</span>
  <span id="freeText2113844088820888881" style="display:none">Mark T. Sullivan (b. 1958) is an author of thrillers. Born in a Boston suburb, he joined the Peace Corp after college, traveling to West Africa to live with a tribe of Saharan nomads. Upon returning to the United States, he took a job at Reuters, beginning a decade-long career in journalism that would eventually lead to a job as an investigative reporter for the San Diego Tribune.<br /><br />Sullivan spent the winter of 1990 living with a group of skiers in Utah and Wyoming, and used the experience as the foundation for his first novel, The Fall Line (1994). In 1995 he published Hard News, a thriller based on his work as a reporter, and a year later he released The Purification Ceremony, which won the WH Smith Award for Best New Talent. His most recent work is Private Games (2012), which he co-authored with James Patterson. Sullivan lives with his family in Montana, where he skis, hunts, and practices martial arts.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2113844088820888881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
